***cutlass.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:cutlass.html>cutlass</a> (70538)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etylcleanup"><span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_French" class="extiw" title="w:Middle French">Middle French</a></span></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="frm">coutelas</i>, from <span class="etylcleanup"><span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">coutel</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">knife</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">-as</i> <i>(augmentative <a href = vnd.unilang:suffix.html>suffix</a>)</i>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<div class="sister-wikipedia sister-project noprint floatright" style="border: 1px solid aaa; font-size: 90%; background: f9f9f9; width: 250px; padding: 4px; text-align: left;"><div style="float: left;"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/44px-Wikipedia-logo.png" decoding="async" width="44" height="44" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/66px-Wikipedia-logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/88px-Wikipedia-logo.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200" /></div></div><div style="margin-left: 60px;">English Wikipedia <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> an article on:<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/cutlass" class="extiw" title="w:cutlass"><a href = vnd.unilang:cutlass.html>cutlass</a></a></b></div></div><span class="interProject"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/cutlass" class="extiw" title="w:cutlass">Wikipedia </a></span></div>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cutlass.html>cutlass</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">cutlasses</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">nautical</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A short sword with a curved blade, and a convex edge; once used by sailors when <a href = vnd.unilang:boarding.html>boarding</a> an enemy ship.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2015</b> September 1,  Sarah J. <a href = vnd.unilang:maas.html>Maas</a>,  <cite>Queen of <a href = vnd.unilang:shadows.html>Shadows</a></cite>, <small>→ISBN</small>:</span><dl><dd></dd></dl></div>
<dl><dd>She could feel Tern’s stare fixed right between her shoulder <a href = vnd.unilang:blades.html>blades</a>, and <a href = vnd.unilang:knew.html>knew</a> he <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> aching to plunge his <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cutlass.html>cutlass</a></b> there.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1851</b> November 14,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herman_Melville" class="extiw" title="w:Herman Melville">Herman Melville</a>,  chapter XII, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moby-Dick" class="extiw" title="w:Moby-Dick">Moby-Dick; or, The Whale</a></cite>, 1st American edition, New York, N.Y. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harper_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Harper (publisher)">Harper amp; Brothers</a>; London: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Bentley_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Richard Bentley (publisher)">Richard Bentley</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/57395299">57395299</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">In vain the <a href = vnd.unilang:captain.html>captain</a> threatened to throw him overboard; suspended a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cutlass.html>cutlass</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a> his naked wrists; Queequeg <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> the son of a King, and Queequeg budged not.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>A similarly shaped tool; a <a href = vnd.unilang:machete.html>machete</a>.</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">cuttoe</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">hanger</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">short sabre</span></li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cutlass.html>cutlass</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">cutlasses</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">cutlassing</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">cutlassed</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To cut back (vegetation) with a <a href = vnd.unilang:cutlass.html>cutlass</a>.</li></ol>
</body>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:cutler.html>cutler</a> (15444)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">coteler</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">knife-maker</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Norman_language" class="extiw" title="w:Anglo-Norman language">Anglo-Norman</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">cuteler</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">coutelier</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">knife-maker</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cutler.html>cutler</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">cutlers</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>One whose business <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> making or dealing in cutlery.</li></ol>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:cybernetica.html>cybernetica</a> (107892)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">cybernetics</i>, possibly based on 1830s <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">cybernétique</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">the art of governing</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">κυβερνητικός</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">kubernētikós</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">good at steering, good pilot</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">κυβερνάω</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">kubernáō</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">I steer, drive, guide, act as a pilot</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. The term <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> coined in 1948 by <a href = vnd.unilang:u.html>U</a>.S. mathematician <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norbert_Wiener" class="extiw" title="w:Norbert Wiener">Norbert <a href = vnd.unilang:wiener.html>Wiener</a></a>.

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:cynisch.html>cynisch</a> (11438)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjective">Adjective</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:cynisch.html>cynisch</a></strong> (<i>comparative</i> <b class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:cynischer.html>cynischer</a></b>, <i>superlative</i> <b class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:meest.html>meest</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:cynisch.html>cynisch</a></b> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn" lang="nl">cynischt</b>)

***cytokine.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:cytokine.html>cytokine</a> (132269)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">cyto-</i> + <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">κίνησις</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">kínēsis</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">movement</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokine.html>cytokine</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>cytokines</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">biochemistry<span class="ib-comma">,</span> immunology</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Any of various small regulatory proteins that regulate the cells of the immune system.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1975</b> July 1,  Bigazzi PE, Yoshida <a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a>, Ward <a href = vnd.unilang:pa.html>Pa</a>, Cohen S.,  “Production of Lymphokine-Like <a href = vnd.unilang:factors.html>Factors</a> (<a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>Cytokines</a>) by Simian Virus 40-Infected and Simian Virus 40-Transformed Cell”, in  <cite>The American Journal of Pathology</cite>, volume 80, number 1, page 69:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Thus, in the case of viral infection, mechanisms of resistance would be threefold, namely, <a href = vnd.unilang:interferon.html>interferon</a> production, the immune response, including both antibody and lymphokine production, and the generation of lymphokine-like substances by the infected cells themselves. These latter substances have <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> defined as <i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>cytokines</a></b></i>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>1991</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:maxine.html>Maxine</a> Gowen, <i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>Cytokines</a></b> and Bone Metabolism</i>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com.au/books?id=LMFC4SEas5MCamp;pg=PA26amp;dq=%22cytokines%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22cytokines%22amp;f=false">page 26</a>,
<dl><dd>A fundamental feature expressed by the <a href = vnd.unilang:vast.html>vast</a> majority of <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>cytokines</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a profound immunomodulatory activity.</dd>
<dd>Many <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>cytokines</a></b>, presently available in pure recombinant form, modify bone cell metabolism.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2012</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:victor.html>Victor</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:r.html>R</a>. Preedy, Ross Hunter (<a href = vnd.unilang:editors.html>editors</a>), <i>Preface</i>, <i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>Cytokines</a></b></i>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com.au/books?id=KAbSBQAAQBAJamp;pg=PR5amp;dq=%22cytokines%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22cytokines%22amp;f=false">page v</a>,
<dl><dd>The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>cytokines</a></b> are generally considered to be a group of peptides secreted by cells of the immune system such as macrophages, lymphocytes and <a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a> cells, although the same peptides may also be secreted by non-immune cells such as neurological <a href = vnd.unilang:tissues.html>tissues</a> and adipocytes.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2013</b>, Errol B. <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>De</a> Souza (editor), <i>Preface</i>, <i>Neurobiology of <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>Cytokines</a></b>: Methods in Neurosciences</i>, Volume 16, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com.au/books?id=hGe2AgAAQBAJamp;pg=PR13amp;dq=%22cytokines%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22cytokines%22amp;f=false">page xiii</a>,
<dl><dd>The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>cytokines</a></b> provide a classic example of products of the immune system which alter brain and endocrine activities. A variety of <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cytokines.html>cytokines</a></b>, including interleukin 1, interleukin 2, interleukin 6, and tumor necrosis factor α, have <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> traditionally associated with peripheral control of the immune system, inflammation, and acute phase response.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
</body>

***daar.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:daar.html>daar</a> (67)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">dâer</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">thār</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*þar</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverb_2">Adverb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:daar.html>daar</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>there</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">with a preposition</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> that</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p>With a preposition, <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:daar.html>daar</a></i> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> used instead of <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dat.html>dat</a></i> to create a pronominal adverb. See also Category:Dutch pronominal adverbs.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ginds.html>ginds</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ginder.html>ginder</a></span></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_terms">Related <a href = vnd.unilang:terms.html>terms</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

<li><span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:er.html>er</a></span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:waar.html>waar</a></span></li></ul>

</p>
<ol><li>since (preceding a reason why something <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> like it <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a>)

***dacks.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:dacks.html>dacks</a> (76559)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Enhanced adverbial form of <i class="Latn mention" lang="lb">déck</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">thick</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Middle High German">Middle High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gmh">dicke</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">thickly; often</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Old High German">Old High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">thicco</i>. Compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dikwijls.html>dikwijls</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">often</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. The vowel <i>-a-</i> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> native, while the <i>-é-</i> of the adjective <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> due to influence by surrounding dialects.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverb">Adverb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="lb"><a href = vnd.unilang:dacks.html>dacks</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>often; frequently</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">dadele</i>. Ultimately from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la"><a href = vnd.unilang:dactylus.html>dactylus</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">δάκτυλος</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">dáktulos</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, with the sense “date” probably deriving from a Semitic language. <span class="maintenance-line"><i>This etymology <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> incomplete. You can help Wiktionary by elaborating on the origins of this term.</i></span>

***dader.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:dader.html>dader</a> (2007)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:daad.html>daad</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:deed.html>deed</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dictatoriaal.html>-er</a></i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dader.html>dader</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:daders.html>daders</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dader.html>dadertje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>, <i>feminine</i> <b class="Latn" lang="nl">daderes</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>doer, perpetrator
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>De</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:dader.html>dader</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:kon.html>kon</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:helaas.html>helaas</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:ontkomen.html>ontkomen</a>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">Unfortunately, the perpetrator managed to escape.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>

***daf.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:daf.html>daf</a> (65525)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etylcleanup"><span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Old High German">Old High German</a></span></span> <i>(*)douv</i>, northern variant of <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">toub</i>, from <span class="etylcleanup"><span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*daubaz</i>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:taub.html>taub</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">deaf</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:doof.html>doof</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Icelandic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Icelandic language">Icelandic</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="is">daufur</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjective">Adjective</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="lb"><a href = vnd.unilang:daf.html>daf</a></strong> (<i>masculine</i> <b class="Latn" lang="lb">dawen</b>, <i>neuter</i> <b class="Latn" lang="lb">daaft</b>, <i>comparative</i> <b class="Latn" lang="lb">méi <a href = vnd.unilang:daf.html>daf</a></b>, <i>superlative</i> <b class="Latn" lang="lb">am daafsten</b>)

***dag.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:dag.html>dag</a> (149)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1_3">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">dach</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt"><a href = vnd.unilang:dag.html>dag</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*dagaz</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_9">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dag.html>dag</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dagen.html>dagen</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dagje.html>dagje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl">daagje</b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>day <span class="gloss-brac">(</span><span class="gloss-content">period of 24 <a href = vnd.unilang:hours.html>hours</a></span><span class="gloss-brac">)</span></li>
<li>daytime <span class="gloss-brac">(</span><span class="gloss-content">time between sunrise and sunset</span><span class="gloss-brac">)</span></li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes_2">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li>In archaic or dialectal usage, the older plural form <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:daag.html>daag</a></i> may occur after numerals. On <a href = vnd.unilang:rare.html>rare</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:occasions.html>occasions</a> the expression <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:veertien.html>veertien</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:daag.html>daag</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">a fortnight</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> still found in contemporary standard Dutch.</li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms_3">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li>(24 <a href = vnd.unilang:hours.html>hours</a>) <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:etmaal.html>etmaal</a></span> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span></li></ul>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Interjection_3">Interjection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dag.html>dag</a></strong>!
</p>
<ol><li>hello, short for <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:goedendag.html>goedendag</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">good day</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> 'goodday; goodbye'</li>
<li>goodbye, same shortening</li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms_4">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">bye</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span><span class="ib-colon sense-qualifier-colon">:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:daag.html>daag</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ciao.html>ciao</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:salut.html>salut</a></span> (French), <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:saluut.html>saluut</a></span> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">Flemish</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl">saluutjes</span> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">Flemish</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:vaarwel.html>vaarwel</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:tot.html>tot</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:ziens.html>ziens</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:tot.html>tot</a> hoors</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:tot.html>tot</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:horens.html>horens</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:doei.html>doei</a></span> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">Netherlands</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:doeg.html>doeg</a></span> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">Netherlands</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span></li>

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2_3">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Unknown
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_10">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dag.html>dag</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dag.html>daggen</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dagje.html>dagje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>A piece of rope, used to punish sailors with, on the spot or in running the gauntlet</li>
<li>A line used to fasten young sailors while training <a href = vnd.unilang:boarding.html>boarding</a> a hostile ship or climbing the rigging</li></ol>

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">dagelics</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">dagawelikis</i>, a compound of <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt"><a href = vnd.unilang:dag.html>dag</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">day</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + the genitive of <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">welik</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">which, whichever, any</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> (modern <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:welk.html>welk</a></i>). ***dagen.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:dagen.html>dagen</a> (356)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">dāgen</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">*<a href = vnd.unilang:dagon.html>dagon</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*dagāną</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dagen.html>dagen</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to dawn</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to light, illuminate, color by lighting</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to rise</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to start, begin</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to begin to become understood</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> law</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to subpoena, summon to appear in court</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to call, summon to battle, notably against uproar</li></ol>

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">dageraet</i>. The further etymology <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> unknown, and <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> not related to <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:raad.html>raad</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">advice</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognates are found in Old High German <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">tagarōt</i>, Old English <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">dæġrēd</i>; suggesting a link to <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:rood.html>rood</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">red</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.

***daisy.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:daisy.html>daisy</a> (4954)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">dayesye</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">dæġes ēage</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:daisy.html>daisy</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span>, literally <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">day's eye</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> due to the flowers closing their blossoms during night. The rhyming <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:comes.html>comes</a> from <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:daisy.html>daisy</a> roots</i> for <i>boots</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:daisy.html>daisy</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">daisies</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A wild flowering plant <i>Bellis perennis</i> of the Asteraceae family, with a yellow head and white petals</li>
<li>Many other flowering plants of various species.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href = vnd.unilang:cockney.html>Cockney</a> rhyming <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A <a href = vnd.unilang:boot.html>boot</a> or other footwear.</li></ol>
</body>
